data-id="article_rights_permissions">Request reuse permissions</a></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_header-metrics-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="article_header-metrics-dropzone"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/medium/nl4c03453_0006.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Huge volume changes of bismuth (Bi) anode leading to rapid capacity hindered its practical application in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). Herein, porous Bi@C (P-Bi@C) microspheres consisting of self-assembled Bi nanosheets and carbon shells were constructed via a hydrothermal method combined with a carbothermic reduction. The optimized P-Bi@C-700 (annealed at 700 °C) demonstrates 359.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1500 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. <i>In situ/ex situ</i> characterization and density functional theory calculations verified that this P-Bi@C-700 relieves the volume expansion, facilitates Na<sup>+</sup>/electron transport, and possesses an alloying-type storage mechanism. Notably, P-Bi@C-700 also achieved 360.8 and 370.3 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup> under 0 and 60 °C conditions, respectively. Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>//P-Bi@C-700 exhibits a capacity of 359.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 260 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. These hierarchical microspheres effectively moderate the volume fluctuation, preserving structural reversibility, thereby achieving superior Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance. This self-template strategy provides insight into designing high-volumetric capacity alloy-based anodes for SIBs.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D15242%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DYan%2BWang%252C%2BYongxin%2BKuang%252C%2BJie%2BCui%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D24%26issueNum%3D48%26contentID%3Dacs.nanolett.4c03453%26title%3DSelf-Template%2BConstruction%2Bof%2BHierarchical%2BBi%2540C%2BMicrospheres%2Bas%2BCompetitive%2BWide%2BTemperature-Operating%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BSuperior%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1530-6984%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dnalefd%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D15251%26publicationDate%3DDecember%2B2024" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2024 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Batteries" class="article__tags__link">Batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292123&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Microspheres" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Microspheres" class="article__tags__link">Microspheres</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292274&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Surface chemistry" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Surface%20chemistry" class="article__tags__link">Surface chemistry</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292275&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Transmission electron microscopy" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Transmission%20electron%20microscopy" class="article__tags__link">Transmission electron microscopy</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Sodium-ion%20batteries">Sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Bi%40c+Anode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Bi%40C%20anode">Bi@C anode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Hierarchical+Microspheres&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Hierarchical%20microspheres">Hierarchical microspheres</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Wide-temperature+Range&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Wide-temperature%20range">Wide-temperature range</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Self-template&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Self-template">Self-template</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><p class="first">Recently, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have overwhelmed the energy storage market due to their high energy density and long cycling life. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1,2)</a> However, the limited lithium salt presents a great challenge for LIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> Therefore, it is urgent to explore alternative systems to partially replace LIBs. Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are a promising candidate for LIBs due to abundant resources and similar electrochemical behaviors. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4 ref5'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref5" aria-label="reference 4 and 5">(4,5)</a> Nevertheless, Na<sup>+</sup> cannot form the corresponding intercalation compounds of graphite. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6 ref7'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6 ref7" aria-label="reference 6 and 7">(6,7)</a> Consequently, it is crucial to explore suitable anode materials for SIBs. Bismuth (Bi) has emerged as a promising candidate for SIBs due to its suitable redox reaction potential, high volumetric energy density (3800 mAh cm<sup>–3</sup>), and superior electronic conductivity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8" aria-label="reference 8">(8)</a> However, the application of the Bi anode faces the challenges of inevitable volume expansion leading to rapid capacity decay. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> To address these issues, various modification methods have been explored, including structural control, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10" aria-label="reference 10">(10)</a> interface engineering, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11" aria-label="reference 11">(11)</a> carbon modification, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12" aria-label="reference 12">(12)</a> designing multicomponent alloys, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8" aria-label="reference 8">(8)</a> and so on.</p><p>Among them, hollow/porous structures have driven extensive attention owing to large surface areas and kinetically favorable open structures allowing for good contact with the electrolyte and rapid diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> Furthermore, they possess suitable void spaces to mitigate the intrinsic stress during  repeated Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction and thus prevent structural collapse. Additionally, carbon coating has been verified as an effective method to improve electronic conductivity and maintain structural integrity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14" aria-label="reference 14">(14)</a> For instance, Xu et al. reported hierarchical Bi@C via pyrolysis of bismuth citrate as an anode for SIBs to effectively mitigate the expansion strain and achieved excellent rate capability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> Yu et al. designed a yolk–shell Bi@void@C nanosphere anode for SIBs, which effectively alleviated the volume expansion and exhibited excellent cycling stability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16" aria-label="reference 16">(16)</a> Moreover, the introduction of N-doped carbon has been verified as an effective method to enhance electronic conductivity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17" aria-label="reference 17">(17)</a> Therefore, it is reasonable to wrap Bi nanoparticles in heteroatom-doped carbon to achieve a high reversible capacity and structural stability. Recently, <i>in situ</i> polymerization of PDA has proven a viable encapsulation technique for achieving N-doped carbon coatings. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21" aria-label="reference 18 to 21">(18−21)</a> Based on the above consideration, the construction of N-doped carbon-encapsulated hierarchical Bi@C microspheres will significantly enhance the rate capability and cycling stability for SIBs.</p><p>Herein, hierarchical Bi@C microspheres (P-Bi@C) were designed using the hydrothermal synthesized (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> as a self-template via <i>in situ</i> coating with polydopamine (PDA) and subsequent carbothermic reduction (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>a). The scanning electron microscopy (SEM) image of precursor (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>b) displayed a well-dispersed microsphere structure consisting of stacked nanosheets with an average diameter of ∼1.82 μm (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>). Transmission electron microscopy (TEM) images revealed that (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> has a microsphere structure with a diameter of ∼2 μm (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>). High-resolution TEM (HRTEM) images with a lattice fringe spacing of 0.295 nm correspond to the (013) crystal plane of (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2b</a>). Additionally, energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDX) element mapping (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2c</a>) revealed an even distribution of C, O, and Bi elements. The P-Bi@C-700 microspheres with an average diameter of 1.79 μm well-inherited the hierarchical structure of the (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> with a N-doped carbon shell on the nanosheet subunit surface (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 1</a>c, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S3</a>). Furthermore, P-Bi@C-600 and P-Bi@C-500 exhibit  hierarchical microsphere structures similar to those of P-Bi@C-700, verifying no obvious influence of the heat treatment temperature on morphology (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 1</a>d-e, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S4</a>, and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S5</a>).</p><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/medium/nl4c03453_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) Schematic illustration of the fabrication procedure for P-Bi@C microspheres. SEM images of (b) (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, (c) P-Bi@C-700, (d) P-Bi@C-600, and (e) P-Bi@C-500. (f) TEM, (g) HRTEM, (h) SEAD, and (i) EDS element mapping signals of the P-Bi@C-700 microsphere.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>The crystal structure information on the (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> and P-Bi@C microspheres was characterized by X-ray diffraction (XRD). As depicted in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6a</a>, the XRD peaks match well  with the standard card (PDF#41-1488), indicating the successful obtainment of (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>. The XRD pattern of the P-Bi@C microspheres (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6b</a>) demonstrated diffraction peaks of metallic Bi (PDF#85-1329), implying a successful reduction of (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> to Bi. The Raman spectrum of the (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>) exhibits two peaks at ∼90 and ∼190 cm<sup>–1</sup> that can be ascribed to Bi and basic bismuth carbonate, respectively. In the Raman spectrum of P-Bi@C (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>), a peak at ∼90 cm<sup>–1</sup> corresponds to the lattice vibration of Bi. Furthermore, two characteristic peaks that appeared at ∼1345 and ∼1591 cm<sup>–1</sup> are attributed to the D-peak and G-peak of the PDA-derived carbon, respectively. The I<sub>D</sub>/I<sub>G</sub> ratios of the P-Bi@C obtained at 500 °C, 600 °C, and 700 °C were 1.28, 1.33, and 1.28, respectively, indicating considerable amorphous carbon with abundant defects. X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) of (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9a</a>) confirms the coexistence of Bi, C, and O. Meanwhile, the P-Bi@C (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10a</a>) contains Bi, C, O, and N elements, indicating successfully introduction of N-doped carbon. In the C 1s spectrum of (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9b</a>) a peak around 288.9 eV corresponds to CO<sub>3</sub><sup>2–</sup>. The binding energies of the Bi 4f peaks, 159.15 eV and 164.45 eV ((BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9c</a>), shift to 158.41 eV and 163.71 eV (P-Bi@C-700, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10b</a>), respectively, indicating that Bi<sup>3+</sup> was successfully reduced to Bi after carbothermic reduction. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14" aria-label="reference 14">(14)</a> The N 1s spectrum of P-Bi@C-700 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10c</a>) showed three peaks located at 398.2, 399.9, and 401.3 eV that belonged to the pyridine-N, pyro-N, and graphitic-N, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> The Bi contents in these P-Bi@C products were measured by thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) and calculated to be 85.21, 85.57, and 86.05 wt %, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11a</a>). The N<sub>2</sub> adsorption/desorption isotherm results of P-Bi@C-700 reveal a specific surface area of 24.23 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup> with an average pore diameter of 6.33 nm (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11b</a>). TEM images of P-Bi@C-700 (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 1</a>f–i) further reveal a microsphere structure with a diameter of ∼1.79 μm, which  well matched  the SEM results (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>). The HRTEM images (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>g) reveal that the Bi nanosheets are enveloped by an ∼12 nm amorphous carbon layer. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>g exhibits a lattice fringe of 0.326 nm that corresponds to the (012) crystal plane of rhombohedral Bi (PDF#85-1329). The selected area electron diffraction (SAED) pattern displays diffraction rings that align with the (012) crystal plane of Bi. Additionally, the corresponding EDX further confirms the homogeneous distribution of C and N elements.</p><p>The Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of these P-Bi@C anodes was investigated within a voltage range of 0.01–1.5 V. The initial five cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a) with reduction peaks located at 0.98 and 0.18 V can be attributed to the formation of the solid electrolyte interface (SEI). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> The second to fifth CV curves with the oxidation/reduction peaks are well overlapped, indicating a highly reversible alloying/dealloying reaction of P-Bi@C-700. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> The galvanostatic charge/discharge (GCD) curves of P-Bi@C-700 appear to have similar voltage plateaus without obvious polarization and achieve 378.9, 358.4, 353.4, 351.1, 350.6, and 348.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> from 0.05 to 2 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 2</a>b,c). The P-Bi@C-700 with initial charge/discharge capacities of 409.6/631.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, has a remaining capacity retention of 92.4% after 60 cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>d). The GCD curves of P-Bi@C-700 (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>e) are well overlapped indicating excellent cycling stability and reversibility. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24 ref25 ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24 ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 24 to 26">(24−26)</a> Notably, the P-Bi@C-700 anode (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>f) maintains a capacity of 359.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1560 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup> with a capacity retention of 93.9%. In contrast, the P-Bi@C-600 and P-Bi@C-500 anodes only achieved 315.1 and 290.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1130 and 1456 cycles, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S12, S13</a>). Additionally, an obvious capacity decay occurs when the salt changes from NaPF<sub>6</sub> to NaClO<sub>4</sub> or the DME solvent changes to ethylene carbonate (EC)/diethyl carbonate (DEC) (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S14, S15</a>). This phenomenon is attributed to the different ionic species and solvents in the electrolyte, resulting in different compositions and structures of the SEI (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S16–S19</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10 ref27 ref34'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref27 ref34" aria-label="reference 10, 27 and 34">(10,27,34)</a> Moreover, compared with the reported Bi-based anodes (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>g and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>), P-Bi@C-700 also exhibits significant advantages in reversible capacity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16 ref26 ref27 ref28 ref29 ref30 ref31 ref32 ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref26 ref27 ref28 ref29 ref30 ref31 ref32 ref33" aria-label="reference 16 and 26 to 33">(16,26−33)</a></p><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/medium/nl4c03453_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance and kinetics analysis of P-Bi@C-700: (a) initial five CV curves; (b) GCD curves and (c) rate performance; (d) cycling performance and (e) GCD curves at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup>; (f) comparison of cycling performance in different electrolytes at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>; (g) comparison of cycle stability with the reported Bi-based anode; (h) CV curves at different scan rates; (i) the fitted b-value of redox peaks; and (j) pseudocapacitive contribution rates at different scan rates. DFT results of Bi@NC, Bi@C, and Bi: (k) Na<sup>+</sup> migration paths and diffusion energy barriers; (l) Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption models and adsorption energy; and (m) DOS.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>To understand the origin of the excellent Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of P-Bi@C-700, a kinetic analysis was performed. As the scan rate changed from 0.1 to 1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>h), the oxidation/reduction peaks of P-Bi@C-700 appear to shift slightly, and the peak current increases significantly. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35" aria-label="reference 35">(35)</a> In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 2</a>i and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S20a</a>, the b-values of the A1, A2, C1, and C2 peaks are calculated to be 0.83, 0.75, 0.99, and 0.95, respectively, suggesting that both pseudocapacitance and diffusion processes contribute to the sodiation/desodiation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36 ref37 ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36 ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 36 to 38">(36−38)</a> The P-Bi@C-700 possesses a high pseudocapacitive contribution ratio of 90%, 93%, 94%, 95%, 96%, and 99% from 0.1 to 1.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 2</a>j, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S20b</a>), indicating its rapid Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics. As displayed in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S21</a>, the charge transfer resistance (Rct) decreased from the 1st to 10th to 50th cycle and eventually reached a relatively stable value, indicating that the SEI can withstand the mechanical strain during sodiation/desodiation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39" aria-label="reference 39">(39)</a> <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S22</a> displays the electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) of P-Bi@C-700 during the initial cycle. The ohmic resistance (R<sub>Ω</sub>) gradually becomes smaller from 1.1 to 0.1 V suggesting that the rapid ion diffusion of the P-Bi@C-700 and the formed NaBi and Na<sub>3</sub>Bi facilitate charge transfer. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> When charging back to 1.5 V, R<sub>ct</sub> reaches a steady state and is associated with the disappearance of the NaBi and Na<sub>3</sub>Bi. Notably, the R<sub>Ω</sub> of the P-Bi@C-700 slightly decreases throughout the cycles, indicating excellent structural stability of these hierarchical microspheres. The Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>) of P-Bi@C-700 calculated by galvanostatic intermittent titration technique is much higher than those of P-Bi@C-600 and P-Bi@C-500, suggesting superior Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S23–S25</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a></p><p>Density functional theory (DFT) calculations were carried out to reveal the interactions of Na<sup>+</sup> with Bi, Bi@C, and Bi@NC. The Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion energy barrier of Bi@NC (0.19 eV) is much lower than those of Bi (0.52 eV) and Bi@C (0.31 eV), suggesting that the N-doped carbon significantly reduces the diffusion resistance (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>k). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42" aria-label="reference 42">(42)</a> <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>l shows that the Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption energies (<i>E</i><sub>ad</sub>) of Bi, Bi@C, and Bi@NC are −0.375, −1.029, and −1.7256 eV, respectively, revealing that the presence of carbon significantly increased the <i>E</i><sub>ad</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" aria-label="reference 43">(43)</a> The corresponding density of states (DOS) curves (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>m) show that the metallic conductivity of Bi is mainly contributed by the Bi 6p orbitals. After carbon coating, the C 2p orbitals further increased the number of conductible electrons of Bi@C. In addition, the N-doped carbon endows more conduction electrons, thus enhancing the electrical conductivity and favoring the diffusion kinetics of the Na<sup>+</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44 ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44 ref45" aria-label="reference 44 and 45">(44,45)</a> These results strongly support the idea that the introduction of N-doped carbon effectively accelerates the reaction kinetics of P-Bi@C.</p><p>The storage mechanism and structural evolution of P-Bi@C microspheres during Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction were revealed by <i>in situ</i> XRD and TEM observations. The initial GCD curves (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>a) with the corresponding <i>in situ</i> XRD (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>b,c) show the characteristic peaks of Bi (27.3°, 38.1°, and 39.8°) dribbled away and new peaks of NaBi (25.8° and 32.0°) emerged during the discharging process. Then the peaks of NaBi disappeared with further discharging, and the peaks (21.1°, 33.1°, and 33.8°) of Na<sub>3</sub>Bi appeared. During the charging process, Na<sub>3</sub>Bi is dealloying to form NaBi and eventually returns to Bi, indicating a symmetrical phase transformation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46" aria-label="reference 46">(46)</a> <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>d illustrates the schematic of the TEM model of P-Bi@C-700 performed <i>in situ</i>. The P-Bi@C-700 experienced huge expansion during initial sodiation with sizes ranging from 0.561 to 0.775 μm (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 3</a>e–g), respectively. The particle size increased to 0.903 μm at the fully discharged state, whereas the carbon layer was without any cracks (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>h). P-Bi@C-700 underwent volume shrinkage during the desodiation process with the particle size decreasing from 0.806 to 0.638 μm, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 3</a>i–k). <i>Ex situ</i> SAED and corresponding HRTEM analyses were performed to investigate the structural evolution. Initially,  P-Bi@C-700 with a crystal lattice of 0.326 nm and corresponding diffraction rings are indexed to the (012) crystal of Bi (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>l). Discharged to 0.67 V, the prominent crystal lattice (0.281 nm) and the corresponding SAED ring can be ascribed to  NaBi (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>m). When discharged to 0.01 V, the lattice stripes (0.423 nm) and the corresponding SAED rings matched well  with those of Na<sub>3</sub>Bi (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>n). The EDS mapping signals of Bi and Na overlapping well further verified the alloying process (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S26, S27</a>). The results obtained from <i>in situ</i> XRD and TEM, <i>ex situ</i> SAED, and EDX patterns provide strong evidence that the P-Bi@C-700 undergoes a reversible alloying/dealloying reaction. As illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>o, the alloying reaction during the discharging/charging can be summarized as follows: <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref47" aria-label="reference 47">(47)</a></p><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-1"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-2"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-3"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-4"><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-5"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-6" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-7">N</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-8">a</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-9" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-10">+</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-11" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-12"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-13" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-14">e</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-15" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-16">−</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-17" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-18"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-19">B</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-20">i</span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-21"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-22" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">↔</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-23"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-24"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-25">N</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-26">a</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-27">B</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-28">i</span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-1"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msup><mrow><mi>N</mi><mi>a</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup><mo>+</mo><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="italic">e</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo></mrow></msup><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>B</mi><mi>i</mi></mrow></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">↔</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mrow><mi>N</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>B</mi><mi>i</mi></mrow></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(1)</span></div></div><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq2"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-29"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-30"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-31"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-32"><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-33"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-34" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-35">2</span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-36"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-37">N</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-38">a</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-39" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-40">+</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-41" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-42">2</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-43"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-44" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-45">e</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-46" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-47">−</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-48" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-49"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-50">N</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-51">a</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-52">B</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-53">i</span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-54"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-55" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">↔</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-56"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-57"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-58" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-59">N</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-60">a</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-61" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-62">3</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-63"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-64">B</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-65">i</span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-2"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msup><mrow><mn>2</mn><mrow><mi>N</mi><mi>a</mi></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup><mo>+</mo><mn>2</mn><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="italic">e</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo></mrow></msup><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>N</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>B</mi><mi>i</mi></mrow></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">↔</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>N</mi><mi>a</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>3</mn></mrow></msub><mrow><mi>B</mi><mi>i</mi></mrow></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(2)</span></div></div><p></p><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/medium/nl4c03453_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism of P-Bi@C-700: (a) Initial GCD curve and (b, c) corresponding <i>in situ</i> XRD. (d) The schematic of <i>in situ</i> TEM characterization. TEM images during (e–h) sodiation and (i–k) desodiation. <i>Ex situ</i> SAED and corresponding HRTEM images at different discharge states: (l) initial, (m) 0.67 V, and (n) 0.01 V. (o) Schematic diagram of alloying/dealloying mechanism.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>To further evaluate the volume fluctuation, the thickness change of the electrode during the initial charge/discharge was carried out by the <i>ex situ</i> cross-sectional SEM. The SEM image of the P-Bi@C-700 abides with well-distributed hierarchical microspheres and conductive carbon with an initial thickness of ∼9.96 μm (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 4</a>a, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S28a</a>). When discharged to 0.45 and 0.01 V (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 4</a>b,c), the thickness of P-Bi@C-700 increased to 13.32 and 21.16 μm with a corresponding volume change of ∼32.8% and 124.9%, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48" aria-label="reference 48">(48)</a> P-Bi@C-700 experienced volume shrinkage during the charging with the thickness reduced to 18.52, 13.37, and 11.76 μm, indicating volume expansion rates of 85.9%, 34.2%, and 18.1%, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 4</a>d–f). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref49" aria-label="reference 49">(49)</a> SEM images at different charging/discharging states (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S28</a>) showed that the integrity structure was well-preserved, revealing the highly structural stability of the P-Bi@C-700. To further evaluate the structural stability, the morphological evolution during the cycling was investigated by <i>ex situ</i> SEM (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S29</a>). After the initial cycle, the electrode surface is covered with an SEI layer, which consumes a significant amount of electrolyte leading to a rapid drop in the initial capacity (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S29b</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50" aria-label="reference 50">(50)</a> As cycles increased, the SEI on the P-Bi@C surface became more homogeneous, and the particles swelled without cracks or rupture of the carbon layer (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S29c</a>). The particle morphology disappeared, reticular nanostructure formed after 10 cycles, and interconnected porous nanostructures stabilized after 50 and 100 cycles, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S29d–f</a>), which provided additional Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion channels and a large electrode–electrolyte contact interface. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref51" aria-label="reference 51">(51)</a> The hierarchical Bi@C remains intact over multiple cycles, facilitating efficient transport of Na<sup>+</sup> electrons, thus improving the Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance.</p><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/medium/nl4c03453_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a–f) Thickness of the P-Bi@C-700 anode at different charge/discharge states. (g) The high-resolution XPS C 1s and F 1s spectra of the P-Bi@C-700 anode after Ar ion sputtering with different depths and (h) corresponding 3D high-resolution XPS spectra maps. (i) TOF-SIMS sputter depth profile of various secondary ion species. (j) The depth view images of the sputtered volume corresponding to the (i) depth profiles. Schematic illustration of (k) the SEI layers and (l) morphological evolution during cycling of P-Bi@C-700.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>The composition of the SEI on  P-Bi@C-700 after 100 cycles was determined by XPS depth investigation and time-of-flight secondary ion mass spectrometry (TOF-SIMS). XPS full-spectrum scans of P-Bi@C-700 cycled in the DME-based electrolyte (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S30</a>) reveal the presence of C, O, Na, F, and P elements. Analysis of the C 1s and O 1s spectra (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S30b–c</a>) shows that the main constituents of the SEI layer are sodium alkoxide (RCH<sub>2</sub>ONa) and polyether. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref51" aria-label="reference 51">(51)</a> The two prominent peaks in the F 1s spectrum (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S30d</a>) correspond to Na–F and P–F bonds resulting from the reduction of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref52" aria-label="reference 52">(52)</a> The characteristic peaks of C–C (284.8 eV), C–O (286.4 eV), and C–F (290.6 and 687.4 eV) decrease dramatically with the increase of etching depth, indicating that organic constituents including the organic fluorine  mainly exist on the surface of the SEI (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 4</a>g,h). As the etching continues, the peak of C–F disappears, while the peak of Na–F (684.2 eV) emerges and is constantly reinforced. The presence of NaF not only increases the strength of the SEI layer but also provides faster channels for Na<sup>+</sup> transporting, thus improving the electrochemical kinetics of the P-Bi@C-700 anode. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref53" aria-label="reference 53">(53)</a> According to the O 1s XPS spectrum (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S31</a>), Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> is mainly dispersed in the outer layer of the SEI, while Na<sub>2</sub>O is more prevalent in the inner layer. The signal intensities of C<sub>2</sub>HO<sup>–</sup>, PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup>, and NaCO<sub>3</sub><sup>–</sup> decreased with increasing sputtering time, while those for NaF<sub>2</sub><sup>–</sup>, NaO<sub>2</sub><sup>–</sup>, and PO<sub>3</sub><sup>–</sup> increased accordingly (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 4</a>i,j, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S32</a>). The potential SEI structure of P-Bi@C-700 is illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>k. Overall, the heterostructures of external organic (organic polyether and inorganic Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>) and internal inorganic (NaF) result in a denser and more stable SEI layer, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref54" aria-label="reference 54">(54)</a> which is conducive to enhanced charge-transfer kinetics leading to superior Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance. The above analysis suggests that the excellent reaction kinetics of  P-Bi@C-700 originated from the formation of stable and thin SEI films that offered more Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion channels and shortened the transport paths.</p><p>To evaluate the performance of P-Bi@C-700 under a wide temperature range, the GCD was measured at 0 and 60 °C, respectively. The Na//P-Bi@C-700 achieves 360.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup>, and corresponding GCD curves (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>b) exhibit similar voltage platforms at 0.69 and 0.49 V. This P-Bi@C-700 exhibits 377.4, 372.8, 362.1, 348.5, 339.3, and 327.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> from 0.05 to 2 A g<sup>–1</sup> at 0 °C, respectively, validating the excellent low-temperature performance (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 5</a>c, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S33</a>). As exhibited in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>d and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S34a</a>, the Na//P-Bi@C-700 possessed 370.3 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> over 50 cycles at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup> under 60 °C. Furthermore, the P-Bi@C-700 maintained 356.4 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 300 cycles, indicating an outstanding high-temperature performance (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>e). When the mixture was returned to 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the capacity of P-Bi@C-700 recovered to 350.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S34b</a>). The GCD curves of the P-Bi@C-700 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S34c</a>) share similar shapes at different rates, further confirming its exceptional rate performance. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S35</a> displays a typical TEM image of P-Bi@C-700 cycled at 60  and 0 °C, which confirms this hierarchical microsphere structure could efficiently palliate the volume change during the Na<sup>+</sup> extraction–insertion process.</p><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/medium/nl4c03453_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a–c) Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of P-Bi@C-700 under 0 °C: (a) cycle performance and (b) GCD curves at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (c) Rate performance from 0.05 to 2.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (d, e) Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of P-Bi@C-700 under 60 °C: (d) cycle performance at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup> and (e) 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (f–j) NVP//P-Bi@C-700 full cell performance: (f) the schematic; (g) GCD curves of P-Bi@C-700, NVP, and NVP//P-Bi@C-700; and (h) CV, (i) GCD curves, and (j) cycling performance at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup> with an inset showing lighted LED bulbs driven by the pouch cell.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/asset/images/large/nl4c03453_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>To comprehensively evaluate the electrochemical performance, a full cell coupled with a Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) cathode and a P-Bi@C-700 anode was assembled and is illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>f. The XRD pattern of the cathode power (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S36a</a>) indicates the typical NVP crystal structure. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref55" aria-label="reference 55">(55)</a> The NVP cathode demonstrates stable charge/discharge voltage platforms at 3.33/3.41 V and 101.34 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 120 cycles at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S36b,c</a>). The NVP//P-Bi@C-700 full cell exhibits two flat discharge platforms at 2.59 and 2.76 V (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>g), which are determined by the difference between the NVP discharge platform (3.33 V) and the P-Bi@C-700 charge platform (0.59 and 0.75 V). Furthermore, CV curves of the NVP//P-Bi@C-700 (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>h) appeared in two pairs of different redox peaks (2.59/2.76 V and 2.72/2.92 V) during the cycling process. The initial GCD curves of the NVP//P-Bi@C-700 (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>i) with overlapped output voltage platforms at ∼2.59 and 2.78 V are matched with the above CV results. As depicted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>j, the full cell achieved 357.3 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 260 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, and the inset NVP//P-Bi@C-700 pouch cell successfully powers “GDUT” LED bulbs.</p><p class="last">In summary, P-Bi@C microspheres were synthesized via a hydrothermal method with a carbothermic reduction. This P-Bi@C-700 attained 359.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1500 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup> and 360.8 and 370.3 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup> for 0 and 60 °C, respectively, verified commendable reversibility in a wide temperature range. Moreover,  Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>//P-Bi@C-700 exhibits 359.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 260 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. <i>In situ</i> XRD/XPS and TOF-SIMs reveal that Bi@C-700 undergoes a typical alloying-type storage mechanism and forms an outer-organic inner-inorganic SEI layer. <i>In situ</i> TEM and DFT calculations verified that these P-Bi@C-700 microspheres effectively relieve the volume expansion and facilitate rapid Na<sup>+</sup>/electron transport, thus preserving highly stable structural reversibility and achieving superior Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance. This self-template synthesis strategy provides valuable insights into the utilization of an alloying-type anode for SIBs.</p><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i4">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Materials, material synthesis, SEM and TEM images, XPS, TGA, Raman spectra, electrochemical characterization, additional electrochemical data, and ToF-SIMS (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453/suppl_file/nl4c03453_si_001.pdf">nl4c03453_si_001.pdf (3.71 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c03453" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Post-lithium-ion battery cell production and its compatibility with lithium-ion cell production infrastructure</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Duffner, Fabian; Kronemeyer, Niklas; Tuebke, Jens; Leker, Jens; Winter, Martin; Schmuch, Richard</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">123-134</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANFD</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium-ion batteries are currently the most advanced electrochem. energy storage technol. due to a favorable balance of performance and cost properties.  Driven by forecasted growth of the elec. vehicles market, the cell prodn. capacity for this technol. is continuously being scaled up.  However, the demand for better performance, particularly higher energy densities and/or lower costs, has triggered research into post-lithium-ion technologies such as solid-state lithium metal, lithium-sulfur and lithium-air batteries as well as post-lithium technologies such as sodium-ion batteries.  Currently, these technologies are being intensively studied with regard to material chem. and cell design.  In this Review, we expand on the current knowledge in this field.  Starting with a market outlook and an anal. of technol. differences, we discuss the manufg. processes of these technologies.  For each technol., we describe anode prodn., cathode prodn., cell assembly and conditioning.  We then evaluate the manufg. compatibility of each technol. with the lithium-ion prodn. infrastructure and discuss the implications for processing costs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqemIGdy2ve37Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liqIN2mQP7onw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXosFersro%253D&amp;md5=310f08459fd24912a78749cae8926fee</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1126/sciadv.aav7412"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Approaching high-performance potassium-ion batteries via advanced design strategies and engineering</span>. <i>Sci. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">5</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1218</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1225</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C7EE03016A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D11%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D1218-1225%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26issue%3D5%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26author%3DX.%2BFan%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26author%3DT.%2BGao%26author%3DS.%2BHou%26author%3DX.%2BZhou%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DF.%2BWang%26author%3DC.%2BYang%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26title%3DIntercalation%2Bof%2BBi%2Bnanoparticles%2Binto%2Bgraphite%2Bresults%2Bin%2Ban%2Bultra-fast%2Band%2Bultra-stable%2Banode%2Bmaterial%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC7EE03016A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC7EE03016A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intercalation of Bi nanoparticles into graphite results in an ultra-fast and ultra-stable anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Ji; Fan, Xiulin; Ji, Xiao; Gao, Tao; Hou, Singyuk; Zhou, Xiuquan; Wang, Luning; Wang, Fei; Yang, Chongyin; Chen, Long; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1218-1225</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been revived as important alternative energy storage devices for large-scale energy storage, which requires SIBs to have a long cycling life and high power d.  However, the scarcity of suitable anode materials hinders their application.  Herein, we report a bismuth intercalated graphite (Bi@Graphite) anode material, which is substantially different from the previously reported metal@Graphene.  In Bi@Graphite, the Bi nanoparticles between graphite interlayers enhance the capacity, while the graphite sheath provides a robust fast electronic connection for long cycling stability.  The Bi@Graphite possesses a safe av. storage potential of approx. 0.5 V vs.  Na/Na+, delivers a capacity of ∼160 mA h g-1 at 1C (160 mA g-1), exhibits outstanding cycling stability (ca. 90% capacity retention for 10 000 cycles at 20C), and can maintain 70% capacity at 300C (∼110 mA h g-1 at 48 A g-1), which is equiv. to full charge/discharge in 12 s.  Bi@Graphite demonstrates the highest rate-capability ever reported among all anodes for SIBs.  Detailed characterization results indicate that the unique Bi nanoparticle-in-graphite structure and the fast kinetics of ether co-intercalation into graphite are responsible for these significant improvements, which could translate into SIBs with excellent power densities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSO-lUIYzLkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liqIN2mQP7onw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXmtVCisrs%253D&amp;md5=fad06b243c2fb803c4692029376e7f13</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201700536"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, C.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Low-cost metallic anode materials for high performance rechargeable batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>31</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">2</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2000756</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202000756</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D31%26publication_year%3D2021%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26issue%3D2%26author%3DW.%2BHong%26author%3DA.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BLi%26author%3DT.%2BQiu%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26author%3DG.%2BZou%26author%3DH.%2BPeng%26author%3DH.%2BHou%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26title%3DBi%2Bdots%2Bconfined%2Bby%2Bfunctional%2Bcarbon%2Bas%2Bhigh-performance%2Banode%2Bfor%2Blithium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.202000756&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.202000756&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bi Dots Confined by Functional Carbon as High-Performance Anode for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Wanwan; Wang, Anni; Li, Lin; Qiu, Tianyun; Li, Jiayang; Jiang, Yunling; Zou, Guoqiang; Peng, Hongjian; Hou, Hongshuai; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000756</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fabrication of Bi/C composites is a common approach to alleviate the severe vol. expansion of Bi alloy-based anodes with a high theor. capacity of 3800 mAh cm-3 for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, the complicated and tedious synthetic routes restrict its large-scale prepn. and practical applications.  Herein, a spongiform porous Bi/C composite (marked as Bi@PC) through the carbothermal redn. (CTR) method is constructed.  Bi nanodots are in situ confined in a porous carbon substrate activated by the gases produced from the decompn. of the sodium phytate precursor, indicating the feasibility and simplicity of this route.  In charge/discharge processes, Bi nanodots embedded in carbon matrix are effective enough to accommodate the strain change and shorten the migration distance.  In addn., the porous carbon forms an efficient conductive network for electron shutting.  When utilized for lithium storage, a superb capacity of 520 mAh g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 after 100 cycles and a satisfying long cyclic stability of 380 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1 after 500 cycles are achieved.  The excellent Li-storage performance and this handy prepn. method jointly make this Bi/C composite a potential anode for LIBs, and could inspire the prepn. of other alloy-type anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBsUEOZulwUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhGXXGxvqXNqw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXntFCksbk%253D&amp;md5=6af6d840ce1aad5e98c61b937f263917</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202116930"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-ion battery with a wide operation-temperature range from – 70 to 100 °C</span>. <i>Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>61</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">13</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e202116930</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.202116930</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D61%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DAngew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%26issue%3D13%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BCao%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26title%3DSodium-ion%2Bbattery%2Bwith%2Ba%2Bwide%2Boperation-temperature%2Brange%2Bfrom%2B%25E2%2580%2593%2B70%2Bto%2B100%2B%25C2%25B0C%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fanie.202116930&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.202116930&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-Ion Battery with a Wide Operation-Temperature Range from -70 to 100 °C</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhi; Zhang, Yu; Zhang, Jianhua; Cao, Yongjie; Chen, Jiawei; Liu, Haimei; Wang, Yonggang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">61</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">e202116930</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), as one of the potential candidates for grid-scale energy storage systems, are required to tackle extreme weather conditions.  However, the all-weather SIBs with a wide operation-temp. range are rarely reported.  Herein, we propose a wide-temp. range SIB, which involves a carbon-coated Na4Fe3(PO4)2P2O7 (NFPP@C) cathode, a bismuth (Bi) anode, and a diglyme-based electrolyte.  We demonstrate that solvated Na+ can be directly stored by the Bi anode via an alloying reaction without the de-solvent process.  Furthermore, the NFPP@C cathode exhibits a high Na+ diffusion coeff. at low temp.  As a result, the Bi//NFPP@C battery exhibits perfect low-temp. behavior.  Even at -70 °C, this battery still delivers 70.19 % of the room-temp. capacity.  Furthermore, benefitting from the high b.p. of the electrolyte, this battery also works well at a high temp. of up to 100 °C.  These results are encouraging for the further exploration of wide-temp. range SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGomH1y_VNTitLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhGXXGxvqXNqw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XislGks7c%253D&amp;md5=ce4975a1558c0ef83e712cc28502797b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202111074"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bridging Evolution of the Solvation Sheath to Rigid-Soft Coupling and Low-Resistance Solid Electrolyte Interface for Fast-Charging and Ultrastable Bi Anode</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unveiling Intrinsic Potassium Storage Behaviors of Hierarchical Nano Bi@N-Doped Carbon Nanocages Framework via In Situ Characterizations</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Zehang; Liu, Yang; Ye, Weibin; Zhang, Jinyang; Wang, Yuyan; Lin, Yue; Hou, Linrui; Wang, Ming-Sheng; Yuan, Changzhou</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">60</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7180-7187</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic bismuth has drawn attention as a promising alloying anode for advanced potassium ion batteries (PIBs).  However, serious vol. expansion/electrode pulverization and sluggish kinetics always lead to its inferior cycling and rate properties for practical applications.  Therefore, advanced Bi-based anodes via structural/compositional optimization and sur-/interface design are needed.  Herein, we develop a bottom-up avenue to fabricate nanoscale Bi encapsulated in a 3D N-doped carbon nanocages (Bi@N-CNCs) framework with a void space by using a novel Bi-based metal-org. framework as the precursor.  With elaborate regulation in annealing temps., the optimized Bi@N-CNCs electrode exhibits large reversible capacities and long-duration cyclic stability at high rates when evaluated as competitive anodes for PIBs.  Insights into the intrinsic K+-storage processes of the Bi@N-CNCs anode are put forward from comprehensive in situ characterizations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGotcuoF939HorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhGXXGxvqXNqw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXktVOksbg%253D&amp;md5=4db97533e4d20441c8bc786855c0f8a3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/eem2.12130"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dang, L.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pam, M.
