                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bismuth Oxide Selenium/Graphene Oxide Composites: Toward High-Performance Electrodes for Aqueous Alkaline Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yi-Lin; Li, Meng-Qiu; Wang, Gui-Gen; Dang, Le-Yang; Li, Fei; Pam, Mei Er; Zhang, Hua-Yu; Han, Jie-Cai; Yang, Hui Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Aq. alk. battery represents a promising energy storage technol. with both high energy d. and high power d. as rechargeable batteries.  However, the low theor. capacities, kinetics and stability of anode materials have limited their developments and commercializations.  In this study, we propose a novel method to produce two-dimensional layered bismuth oxide selenium (Bi2O2Se) and reduced graphene oxide (rGO) composites via a one-step hydrothermal method.  The vol. change caused by phase change during rapid charging and discharging is significantly reduced and the capacity reaches 263.83 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1.  The Bi2O2Se/rGO electrode exhibits excellent cycling stability in which the capacity retention rate is 81.04% after 5000 cycles.  More importantly, the Bi2O2Se/rGO nanosheet composite is used as the anode electrode material with MnCo2O4.5@Ni(OH)2 as the cathode electrode material in aq. alk. battery.  When the energy d. is 76.16 W h kg-1, the power d. reaches 308.65 W kg-1.  At a power d. of 10.21 kW kg-1, the energy d. remains as high as 33.86 W h kg-1.  The results presented here may advance the understanding of the issues facing the development of aq. battery anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4opNMgMfcKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljiDklTw9QvMQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhvVaisrrL&amp;md5=1347908192562026e880a0ee2b835e39</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202401833"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huo, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile galvanic replacement construction of Bi@C nanosheets array as binder-free anodes for superior sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bismuth Nanoparticle@Carbon Composite Anodes for Ultralong Cycle Life and High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Peixun; Bai, Panxing; Li, Ang; Li, Benfang; Cheng, Mingren; Chen, Yiping; Huang, Shuping; Jiang, Qiang; Bu, Xian-He; Xu, Yunhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1904771</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bi has emerged as a promising anode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs), owing to its high capacity and suitable operating potential.  However, large vol. changes during alloying/dealloying processes lead to poor cycling performance.  Here, Bi nanoparticle@C (Bi@C) composite is prepd. via a facile annealing method using a com. coordination compd. precursor of Bi citrate.  The composite has a uniform structure with Bi nanoparticles embedded within a C framework.  The nanosized structure ensures a fast kinetics and efficient alleviation of stress/strain caused by the vol. change, and the resilient and conductive C matrix provides an interconnected electron transportation pathway.  The Bi@C composite delivers outstanding Na-storage performance with an ultralong cycle life of 30,000 cycles at a high c.d. of 8 A/g and an excellent rate capability of 71% capacity retention at an ultrahigh current rate of 60 A/g.  Even at a high mass loading of 11.5 mg/cm2, a stable reversible capacity of 280 mAh/g can be obtained after 200 cycles.  Full SIBs by pairing with a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode demonstrates superior performance.  Combining the facile synthesis and the com. precursor, the exceptional performance makes the Bi@C composite very promising for practical large-scale applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGphFbJVR5Fy-rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljiDklTw9QvMQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insight into the Synergistic Effect of N, S Co-Doping for Carbon Coating Layer on Niobium Oxide Anodes with Ultra-Long Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Xing; Ran, Fanmin; Huang, Yanfei; Zheng, Runtian; Yu, Haoxiang; Shu, Jie; Xie, Ying; He, Yan-Bing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Multi-heteroatoms co-doped carbon coating can significantly enhance the electronic cond. and mass transfer rate of the electrode materials due to the synergistic effect.  In this study N, S co-doped carbon coating is introduced on the surface of niobium oxides (GNO@NSC) by using a convenient thiourea evapn. method.  Theory calcns. and exptl. results confirm the synergistic effect of N, S co-doping in GNO@NSC composite.  N, S co-doping not only enlarges the layer distance of the carbon materials but also leads to more activation sites for lithium storage; meanwhile, the introduction of the co-doping carbon layer on GNO significantly enhances the bonding interaction with GNO, leading to excellent structural stability and cond. of the composite.  As a result, the GNO@NSC composite possesses excellent structural reversibility, a large specific capacity, and high-rate performance.  GNO@NSC nanowires deliver a highly reversible capacity of 288 mAh g-1 and display excellent cycling stability, and its capacity retention is 78.9% after 6000 cycles at a high c.d. of 1 A g-1.  This study reveals the functional mechanism of N, S co-doped carbon coating and the origin of performance improvement of niobium oxides, which can be used for ref. to design and develop relevant materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5epi5um-ry7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljiDklTw9QvMQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXls1WjtrY%253D&amp;md5=8ec0794df426ff7add2a001804f25a59</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/advs.202200247"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zuo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-Sacrifice template construction of uniform yolk-shell ZnS@C for superior alkali-ion storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-Sacrifice Template Construction of Uniform Yolk-Shell ZnS@C for Superior Alkali-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xijun; Li, Fangkun; Zhang, Dechao; Liu, Zhengbo; Zuo, Shiyong; Zeng, Zhiyuan; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Secondary batteries have been widespread in the daily life causing an ever-growing demand for long-cycle lifespan and high-energy alkali-ion batteries.  As an essential constituent part, electrode materials with superior electrochem. properties play a vital role in the battery systems.  Here, an outstanding electrode of yolk-shell ZnS@C nanorods is developed, introducing considerable void space via a self-sacrificial template method.  Such carbon encapsulated nanorods moderate integral electronic cond., thus ensuring rapid alkali-ions/electrons transporting.  Furthermore, the porous structure of these nanorods endows enough void space to mitigate vol. stress caused by the insertion/extn. of alkali-ions.  Due to the unique structure, these yolk-shell ZnS@C nanorods achieve superior rate performance and cycling performance (740 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 after 540 cycles) for lithium-ion batteries.  As a potassium-ion batteries anode, they achieve an ultra-long lifespan delivering 211.1 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 after 5700 cycles.  The kinetic anal. reveals that these ZnS@C nanorods with considerable pseudocapacitive contribution benefit the fast lithiation/delithiation.  Detailed transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and X-ray diffraction (XRD) analyses indicate that such yolk-shell ZnS@C anode is a typical reversible conversion reaction mechanism accomplished by alloying processes.  This rational design strategy opens a window for the development of superior energy storage materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsbXOwk52PPLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg2NfD521l3Xw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Molybdenum oxynitride atomic nanoclusters bonded in nanosheets of N-doped carbon hierarchical microspheres for efficient sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Xiaona; Xi, Baojuan; Lu, Huibing; Zhang, Zhengchunyu; An, Xuguang; Liu, Jie; Feng, Jinkui; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano-Micro Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal nitrides have attracted considerable attention as great potential anode materials due to their excellent metallic cond. and high theor. specific capacity.  However, their cycling performance is impeded by their instability caused by the reaction mechanism.  Herein, we report the engineering and synthesis of a novel hybrid architecture composed of MoO2.0N0.5 at. nanoclusters bonded in nanosheets of N-doped carbon hierarchical hollow microspheres (MoO2.0N0.5/NC) as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The facile self-templating strategy for the synthesis of MoO2.0N0.5/NC involves chem. polymn. and subsequent one-step calcination treatments.  The design is beneficial to improve the electrochem. kinetics, buffer the vol. variation of electrodes during cycling, and provide more interfacial active sites for sodium uptake.  Due to these unique structural and compositional merits, these MoO2.0N0.5/NC exhibits excellent sodium storage performance in terms of superior rate capability and stable long cycle life.  The work shows a feasible and effective way to design novel host candidates and solve the long-term cycling stability issues for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrTY3XbFGOohLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg2NfD521l3Xw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In-Situ Synthesis of Carbon-Encapsulated Atomic Cobalt as Highly Efficient Polysulfide Electrocatalysts for Highly Stable Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Zhuosen; Shen, Jiadong; Xu, Xijun; Yuan, Jujun; Zuo, Shiyong; Liu, Zhengbo; Zhang, Dechao; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-sulfur (Li-S) batteries have been considered as one of the most promising electrochem. energy storage systems because of their high energy d.  However, a series of issues severely limit the practical performances of Li-S batteries such as low cond., significant vol. change, and shuttle effect.  The hollow carbon spheres with huge voids and high elec. cond. are promising as sulfur hosts.  Unfortunately, the nonpolar nature of carbon materials cannot prevent the shuttle effect effectively.  In this case, the at. cobalt is introduced to a nitrogen-doped hollow carbon sphere (ACo@HCS) through polymn. and controlled pyrolysis.  The at. cobalt dopants not only act as active sites to restrict the shuttle effect, but also can promote the kinetics of the sulfur redox reactions.  ACo@HCS acting as sulfur host exhibits a high discharge capacity (1003 mAh g-1) at a 1.0 C rate after 500 cycles, and the corresponding decay rate is as low as 0.002% per cycle.  This exciting work paves a new way to design high-performance Li-S batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpv2JbNHpXPVrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg2NfD521l3Xw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XjsFCmsb0%253D&amp;md5=7c1d6ea33b797f7800fd6a7b7c124dcc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202100654"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In-situ nano-crystallization and solvation modulation to promote highly stable anode involving alloy/de-alloy for potassium ion batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomically dispersed Ni induced by ultrahigh N-doped carbon enables stable sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Keming; Liu, Jiefei; Dai, Hongliu; Zhao, Yong; Sun, Shuhui; Zhang, Jiyu; Qin, Changdong; Yan, Pengfei; Guo, Fengqi; Wang, Caiyun; Cao, Yuliang; Li, Shunfang; Chen, Weihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2684-2694</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHEMVE</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2451-9294</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Cell Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Building phase interface with enough solid-phase contact is of great importance for improving chem. reaction kinetics and depth.  High dispersion of electrode materials, esp. at the at.-level, are known for high interface contact, yet their potential application in batteries is restricted due to low loading.  Herein, the atomically dispersed metal Ni (Ni in Ni-N-C is 54.9 wt %) with high loading was achieved by ultrahigh N-doping carbon (N/N-C:29.5 wt %) during the discharging process of nickel sulfide, leading to good reversibility and high-capacity maintenance owing to ultrahigh phase contact during long cycling for sodium-ion batteries.  It delivers a stable cycling life (0.061% capacity decay per cycle) compared with the poor cyclability (0.418%) for the Ni agglomeration electrode with lower N-doping.  The assembled pouch cells achieve robust stability (92.1% after 50 cycles).  DFT calcns. reveal that ultrahigh N-doping and electrochem. formed Na2S can provide thermally stable Na2S/Ni/NC structures, inhibiting Ni agglomeration during cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5B_IpiJ6Ls7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg2NfD521l3Xw"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1021/acsenergylett.0c00148</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D766-776%26journal%3DACS%2BEnergy%2BLett.%26issue%3D3%26author%3DL.%2BZhou%26author%3DZ.%2BCao%26author%3DW.%2BWahyudi%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.-Y.%2BHwang%26author%3DY.%2BCheng%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BCavallo%26author%3DT.%2BAnthopoulos%26author%3DY.-K.%2BSun%26title%3DElectrolyte%2Bengineering%2Benables%2Bhigh%2Bstability%2Band%2Bcapacity%2Balloying%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Bsodium%2Band%2Bpotassium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsenergylett.0c00148&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsenergylett.0c00148&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolyte Engineering Enables High Stability and Capacity Alloying Anodes for Sodium and Potassium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Lin; Cao, Zhen; Wahyudi, Wandi; Zhang, Jiao; Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Cheng, Yong; Wang, Limin; Cavallo, Luigi; Anthopoulos, Thomas; Sun, Yang-Kook; Alshareef, Husam N.; Ming, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">766-776</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AELCCP</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2380-8195</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of sodium and potassium ion batteries with greater energy d. is gaining great attention.  Although recently proposed alloying anodes (e.g., Sn and Bi) demonstrate much higher capacity than classic carbon anodes, their severe capacity fading hinders their practical applications.  The failure mechanism has traditionally been attributed to the large volumetric change and/or their fragile solid electrolyte interphase (SEI).  However, herein a completely new concept and approach are presented based on electrolyte engineering to stabilize alloying anodes.  This approach results in unprecedented high capacity (&gt; 650 mAh g-1) and stability (&gt; 500 cycles) of alloying anodes by simply tuning the electrolyte compns., without the need for nanostructural control and/or carbon modification.  It is confirmed that the cation solvation structure, particularly the type and location of the anions in the electrolyte, plays a crit. role in alloying anode stabilization.  A new anionic and alloying anode reaction model is presented showing that the root cause of the capacity fading in these alloys is dictated by the properties of the anions and not only the vol. change or fragile SEI effect.  Our model elucidates the failure mechanism in alloying anodes and provides a new guideline for electrolyte design that stabilizes alloying anodes in emerging mobile ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvlve8l8FFQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg2NfD521l3Xw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Integrating Bi@C Nanospheres in Porous Hard Carbon Frameworks for Ultrafast Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Yazhan; Song, Ning; Zhang, Zhengchunyu; Chen, Weihua; Feng, Jinkui; Xi, Baojuan; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">28</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2202673</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have emerged as an alternative technol. because of their merits in abundance and cost.  Realizing their real applications, however, remains a formidable challenge.  One is that among the limitations of anode materials, the alloy-type candidates tolerate fast capacity fading during cycling.  Here, a 3D framework superstructure assembled with carbon nanobelt arrays decorated with a metallic bismuth (Bi) nanospheres coated carbon layer by thermolysis of Bi-based metal-org. framework nanorods is synthesized as an anode material for SIBs.  Due to the unique structural superiority, the anode design promotes excellent sodium-storage performance in terms of high capacity, excellent cycling stability, and ultrahigh rate capability up to 80 A g-1 with a capacity of 308.8 mAh g-1.  The unprecedented sodium-storage ability is not only attributed to the unique hybrid architecture, but also to the prodn. of a homogeneous and thin solid electrolyte interface layer and the formation of uniform porous nanostructures during cycling in the ether-based electrolyte.  Importantly, deeper understanding of the underlying cause of the performance improvement is illuminated, which is vital to provide the theor. basis for application of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgzWKbs82Y-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvWd_oTJYJrA"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1002/smll.202302071</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D19%26publication_year%3D2023%26journal%3DSmall%26issue%3D35%26author%3DX.%2BZhang%26author%3DX.%2BQiu%26author%3DJ.%2BLin%26author%3DZ.%2BLin%26author%3DS.%2BSun%26author%3DJ.%2BYin%26author%3DH.%2BN.%2BAlshareef%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26title%3DStructure%2Band%2Binterface%2Bengineering%2Bof%2Bultrahigh-rate%2B3D%2Bbismuth%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmll.202302071&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmll.202302071&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure and Interface Engineering of Ultrahigh-Rate 3D Bismuth Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Xiaoshan; Qiu, Xueqing; Lin, Jinxin; Lin, Zehua; Sun, Shirong; Yin, Jian; Alshareef, Husam N.; Zhang, Wenli</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">35</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2302071</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted tremendous attention as promising low-cost energy storage devices in future grid-scale energy management applications.  Bismuth is a promising anode for SIBs due to its high theor. capacity (386 mAh g-1).  Nevertheless, the huge vol. variation of Bi anode during (de)sodiation processes can cause the pulverization of Bi particulates and rupture of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI), resulting in quick capacity decay.  It is demonstrated that rigid carbon framework and robust SEI are two essentials for stable Bi anodes.  A lignin-derived carbonlayer wrapped tightly around the bismuth nanospheres provides a stable conductive pathway, while the delicate selection of linear and cyclic ether-based electrolytes enable robust and stable SEI films.  These two merits enable the long-term cycling process of the LC-Bi anode.  The LC-Bi composite delivers outstanding sodium-ion storage performance with an ultra-long cycle life of 10 000 cycles at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1 and an excellent rate capability of 94% capacity retention at an ultrahigh c.d. of 100 A g-1.  Herein, the underlying origins of performance improvement of Bi anode are elucidated, which provides a rational design strategy for Bi anodes in practical SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpzzmQNBhmX3rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvWd_oTJYJrA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Expeditious electrochemical synthesis of mesoporous chalcogenide flakes of copper selenide as high-rate potential anode for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nagaura, Tomota; Li, Jinliang; Fernando, Joseph F. S.; Ashok, Aditya; Alowasheeir, Azhar; Nanjundan, Ashok Kumar; Lee, Sukho; Golberg, Dmitri V.; Na, Jongbeom; Yamauchi, Yusuke</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanostructured copper selenide (Cu2Se) attracts much interest as it shows outstanding performance as thermoelec., photo-thermal, and optical material.  The mesoporous structure is also a promising morphol. to obtain better performance for electrochem. and catalytic applications, thanks to its high surface area.  A simple one-step electrochem. method is proposed for mesoporous chalcogenides synthesis.  The synthesized Cu2Se material has two types of mesopores (9 and 18 nm in diam.), which are uniformly distributed inside the flakes.  These materials are also implemented for sodium (Na) ion battery (NIB) anode as a proof of concept.  The electrode employing the mesoporous Cu2Se exhibits superior and more stable specific capacity as a NIB anode compared to the non-porous samples.  The electrode also exhibits excellent rate tolerance at each c.d., from 100 to 1000 mA g-1.  It is suggested that the mesoporous structure is advantageous for the insertion of Na ions inside the flakes.  Electrochem. anal. indicates that the mesoporous electrode possesses more prominent diffusion-controlled kinetics during the sodiation-desodiation process, which contributes to the improvement of Na-ion storage performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoVM-JdCug5rrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvWd_oTJYJrA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XitVChsLvN&amp;md5=8ce95dd420a777bfb426c41e83b82bc6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1126/sciadv.abq6321"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">West, P.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolytic bismuth/carbon nanotubes composites for high-performance sodium-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zuojun; Li, Xianyang; Qu, Jiakang; Zhao, Zhuqing; Xie, Hongwei; Yin, Huayi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">496</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">229830</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth (Bi) is an attractive anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its unique structure, large lattice spacing along c-axis (d(003) = 3.95 Å), and high volumetric capacity (3800 mAh·cm-3).  However, like other alloy-type anodes (such as Antimony (Sb), Tin (Sn), Germanium (Ge)), the pulverization of Bi due to severe vol. expansion (≈250%) after sodiation results in instability and degrdn. of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) as well as rapid capacity fade.  Here, a Bismuth/Carbon Nanotubes (Bi/CNTs) composite anode is prepd. by one-step electro-deoxidn. to address such issues.  The electrolytic micro-Bi/CNTs composite relieves the effect of vol. expansion and thereby improves its cycling performance.  The capacity of Bi/CNTs is 381.6 mAh·g-1 at 2.0 A·g-1 with a capacity retention of 99.5% after 1000 cycles, which corresponds to a capacity fade of 0.0005% per cycle.  Therefore, this paper shows a green approach to prep. Bi/CNTs composite anode with advantages of the low-cost bismuth trioxide (Bi2O3) feedstocks as well as the synergetic effect between electrolytic Bi and CNTs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpVOM0QCDASb7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLj4unKQH7KQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXns1CnsLc%253D&amp;md5=eef056b13bae3f164482176ddbc9a2bc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202104167"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding and calibration of charge storage mechanism in cyclic voltammetry curves</span>. <i>Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Noticeable pseudo-capacitance behavior out of charge storage mechanism (CSM) has attracted intensive studies because it can provide both high energy d. and large output power.  Although cyclic voltammetry is recognized as the feasible electrochem. technique to det. it quant. in the previous works, the results are inferior due to uncertainty in the definitions and application conditions.  Herein, three successive treatments, including de-polarization, de-residual and de-background, as well as a nonlinear fitting algorithm are employed for the 1st time to calibrate the different CSM contribution of three typical cathode materials, LiFePO4, LiMn2O4 and Na4Fe3(PO4)2P2O7, and achieve well-sepd. phys. capacitance, pseudo-capacitance and diffusive contributions to the total capacity.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dynamic template directed construction of three-dimensional porous bismuth aerogels for high-rate Na-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yani; Wang, Yu; Wang, Haoqiang; Dou, Shuming; Tian, Huijie; Gan, Wei; Yuan, Qunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5945-5955</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Aiming to achieve a metallic bismuth (Bi) anode with const. accommodation of vol. change, a dynamic template strategy is proposed for fabrication of a highly adjustable Bi aerogel anode.  In the presence of the NaBH4 reductant, the in situ generated hydrogen bubbles served as dynamic templates to direct the redn., nucleation and growth of Bi nanoparticles, which are subsequently merged into a three-dimensional porous skeleton.  The unique 3D porous Bi skeleton ensures the rapid alloying/de alloying of sodium ions and efficient electrolyte infiltration.  Its excellent structural integrity and buffering capacity for vol. fluctuation lead to superior rate performance (330.6 mA h g-1 at 30C) and long-term stability (339.1 mA h g-1 after 2000 cycles at 10C) in a half cell.  When coupled with a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode, the Na3V2(PO4)3//Bi full cell exhibits appealing energy d. and power d.  This work demonstrates a new idea for constructing highly reliable alloy-type anodes for high-rate energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFId2YJcXKLLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLj4unKQH7KQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXktVegtrY%253D&amp;md5=71649db8fc4ca3a8e2d6cb4d615394ab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202315076"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A fast Na-ion conduction polymer electrolyte via triangular synergy strategy for quasi-solid-state batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quantum-Matter Bi/THeterostructure Embedded in N-Doped Porous Carbon Nanosheets for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Man; Xi, Baojuan; Shi, Nianxiang; Feng, Jinkui; Qian, Yitai; Xue, Dongfeng; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Structures</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000085</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SSMTB2</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2688-4062</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Combining the strength of heterostructure engineering with the properties of quantum materials, quantum-scale heterostructure will open up a new stage for material design.  Herein, a kind of anode material with heterostructures made of Bi/TiO2 quantum dots embedded into N-doped carbon nanosheets (Bi/TiO2 HQDs⊂NC) is reported.  Importantly, unique electronic states, structural distortions and defects, and functionalities can be integrated in the quantum-scale heterostructure, giving rise to opportunities for reducing the ion-diffusion resistance and facilitating interfacial charge transport at interface during the storage process.  The integrated design greatly reduces the migration energy barrier of Na+, promotes the electron/Na+ transportation, buffers the vol. variation of electrodes upon cycling, heightens the elec. cond. and electrochem. reactivity of the hybrids, and provides rich active interfacial sites for sodium uptake.  Due to these merits, these Bi/TiO2 HQDs⊂NC hybrid nanosheets manifest excellent sodium storage properties in terms of a high reversible capacity of 299.1 at 0.2 A g-1 with an ultrahigh rate capability up to 20 A g-1 with a capacity of 132.7 mAh g-1 and an ultralong cycle life over 10 000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWWf98OBaxS7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6Clb7ngWTbg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xit1ensr8%253D&amp;md5=0c3c41b36e09b36d5cecdc9b8ad21d95</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2020.02.023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mehmood, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Koyutürk, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pampel, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, K.                 10.1002/aenm.201703288</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2018%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26issue%3D15%26author%3DQ.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BMao%26author%3DW.%2BK.%2BPang%26author%3DT.%2BZheng%26author%3DV.%2BSencadas%26author%3DY.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26title%3DBoosting%2Bthe%2Bpotassium%2Bstorage%2Bperformance%2Bof%2Balloy-based%2Banode%2Bmaterials%2Bvia%2Belectrolyte%2Bsalt%2Bchemistry%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.201703288&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.201703288&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202102368"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultra-high initial coulombic efficiency induced by interface engineering enables rapid, stable sodium storage</span>. <i>Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>60</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">20</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">11481</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">11486</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.202102368</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D60%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D11481-11486%26journal%3DAngew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%26issue%3D20%26author%3DY.%2BWan%26author%3DK.%2BSong%26author%3DW.%2BChen%26author%3DC.%2BQin%26author%3DX.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DH.%2BDai%26author%3DZ.%2BHu%26author%3DP.%2BYan%26author%3DC.%2BLiu%26author%3DS.%2BSun%26author%3DS.-L.%2BChou%26author%3DC.%2BShen%26title%3DUltra-high%2Binitial%2Bcoulombic%2Befficiency%2Binduced%2Bby%2Binterface%2Bengineering%2Benables%2Brapid%252C%2Bstable%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fanie.202102368&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.202102368&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultra-High Initial Coulombic Efficiency Induced by Interface Engineering Enables Rapid, Stable Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wan, Yanhua; Song, Keming; Chen, Weihua; Qin, Changdong; Zhang, Xixue; Zhang, Jiyu; Dai, Hongliu; Hu, Zhe; Yan, Pengfei; Liu, Chuntai; Sun, Shuhui; Chou, Shu-Lei; Shen, Changyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">60</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11481-11486</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High initial coulombic efficiency is highly desired because it implies effective interface construction and few electrolyte consumption, indicating enhanced batteries life and power output.  In this work, a high-capacity sodium storage material with FeS2 nanoclusters (≈1-2 nm) embedded in N, S-doped carbon matrix (FeS2/N,S-C) was synthesized, the surface of which displays defects-repaired characteristic and detectable dot-matrix distributed Fe-N-C/Fe-S-C bonds.  After the initial discharging process, the uniform ultra-thin NaF-rich (≈6.0 nm) solid electrolyte interphase was obtained, thereby achieving verifiable ultra-high initial coulombic efficiency (≈92%).  The defects-repaired surface provides perfect platform, and the catalysis of dot-matrix distributed Fe-N-C/Fe-S-C bonds to the rapid decompg. of NaSO3CF3 and diethylene glycol di-Me ether successfully accelerate the building of two-dimensional ultra-thin solid electrolyte interphase.  DFT calcns. further confirmed the catalysis mechanism.  As a result, the constructed FeS2/N,S-C provides high reversible capacity (749.6 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1) and outstanding cycle stability (92.7%, 10 000 cycles, 10.0 A g-1).  Esp., at -15°C, it also obtains a reversible capacity of 211.7 mAh g-1 at 10.0 A g-1.  Assembled pouch-type cell performs potential application.  The insight in this work provides a bright way to interface design for performance improvement in batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqdz922sKlabVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6Clb7ngWTbg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXotlGmtLo%253D&amp;md5=bca4bef4cf87531138ee24ae7202bf92</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1002/advs.202203552"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Crystallinity tuning of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>: unlocking sodium storage capacity and inducing pseudocapacitance behavior</span>. <i>Adv. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">4</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2203552</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/advs.202203552</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2023%26journal%3DAdv.%2BSci.%26issue%3D4%26author%3DH.%2BMa%26author%3DB.%2BZhao%26author%3DJ.%2BBai%26author%3DP.%2BWang%26author%3DW.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BMao%26author%3DX.%2BZhu%26author%3DZ.%2BSheng%26author%3DX.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BSun%26title%3DCrystallinity%2Btuning%2Bof%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%253A%2Bunlocking%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%2Bcapacity%2Band%2Binducing%2Bpseudocapacitance%2Bbehavior%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadvs.202203552&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03453&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadvs.202203552&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Post-lithium-ion battery cell production and its compatibility with lithium-ion cell production infrastructure</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Duffner, Fabian; Kronemeyer, Niklas; Tuebke, Jens; Leker, Jens; Winter, Martin; Schmuch, Richard</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium-ion batteries are currently the most advanced electrochem. energy storage technol. due to a favorable balance of performance and cost properties.  Driven by forecasted growth of the elec. vehicles market, the cell prodn. capacity for this technol. is continuously being scaled up.  However, the demand for better performance, particularly higher energy densities and/or lower costs, has triggered research into post-lithium-ion technologies such as solid-state lithium metal, lithium-sulfur and lithium-air batteries as well as post-lithium technologies such as sodium-ion batteries.  Currently, these technologies are being intensively studied with regard to material chem. and cell design.  In this Review, we expand on the current knowledge in this field.  Starting with a market outlook and an anal. of technol. differences, we discuss the manufg. processes of these technologies.  For each technol., we describe anode prodn., cathode prodn., cell assembly and conditioning.  We then evaluate the manufg. compatibility of each technol. with the lithium-ion prodn. infrastructure and discuss the implications for processing costs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqemIGdy2ve37Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgApPv_8ozbaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXosFersro%253D&amp;md5=310f08459fd24912a78749cae8926fee</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1126/sciadv.aav7412"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Approaching high-performance potassium-ion batteries via advanced design strategies and engineering</span>. <i>Sci.                 10.1039/C7EE03016A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intercalation of Bi nanoparticles into graphite results in an ultra-fast and ultra-stable anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Ji; Fan, Xiulin; Ji, Xiao; Gao, Tao; Hou, Singyuk; Zhou, Xiuquan; Wang, Luning; Wang, Fei; Yang, Chongyin; Chen, Long; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1218-1225</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been revived as important alternative energy storage devices for large-scale energy storage, which requires SIBs to have a long cycling life and high power d.  However, the scarcity of suitable anode materials hinders their application.  Herein, we report a bismuth intercalated graphite (Bi@Graphite) anode material, which is substantially different from the previously reported metal@Graphene.  In Bi@Graphite, the Bi nanoparticles between graphite interlayers enhance the capacity, while the graphite sheath provides a robust fast electronic connection for long cycling stability.  The Bi@Graphite possesses a safe av. storage potential of approx. 0.5 V vs.  Na/Na+, delivers a capacity of ∼160 mA h g-1 at 1C (160 mA g-1), exhibits outstanding cycling stability (ca. 90% capacity retention for 10 000 cycles at 20C), and can maintain 70% capacity at 300C (∼110 mA h g-1 at 48 A g-1), which is equiv. to full charge/discharge in 12 s.  Bi@Graphite demonstrates the highest rate-capability ever reported among all anodes for SIBs.  Detailed characterization results indicate that the unique Bi nanoparticle-in-graphite structure and the fast kinetics of ether co-intercalation into graphite are responsible for these significant improvements, which could translate into SIBs with excellent power densities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSO-lUIYzLkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lin6Yi7tG2Cuw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXmtVCisrs%253D&amp;md5=fad06b243c2fb803c4692029376e7f13</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201700536"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, C.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Low-cost metallic anode materials for high performance rechargeable batteries</span>. <i>Adv.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fabrication of Bi/C composites is a common approach to alleviate the severe vol. expansion of Bi alloy-based anodes with a high theor. capacity of 3800 mAh cm-3 for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, the complicated and tedious synthetic routes restrict its large-scale prepn. and practical applications.  Herein, a spongiform porous Bi/C composite (marked as Bi@PC) through the carbothermal redn. (CTR) method is constructed.  Bi nanodots are in situ confined in a porous carbon substrate activated by the gases produced from the decompn. of the sodium phytate precursor, indicating the feasibility and simplicity of this route.  In charge/discharge processes, Bi nanodots embedded in carbon matrix are effective enough to accommodate the strain change and shorten the migration distance.  In addn., the porous carbon forms an efficient conductive network for electron shutting.  When utilized for lithium storage, a superb capacity of 520 mAh g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 after 100 cycles and a satisfying long cyclic stability of 380 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1 after 500 cycles are achieved.  The excellent Li-storage performance and this handy prepn. method jointly make this Bi/C composite a potential anode for LIBs, and could inspire the prepn. of other alloy-type anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBsUEOZulwUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lin6Yi7tG2Cuw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXntFCksbk%253D&amp;md5=6af6d840ce1aad5e98c61b937f263917</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202116930"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-ion battery with a wide operation-temperature range from – 70 to 100 °C</span>. <i>Angew.                         rightTab-cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-Ion Battery with a Wide Operation-Temperature Range from -70 to 100 °C</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhi; Zhang, Yu; Zhang, Jianhua; Cao, Yongjie; Chen, Jiawei; Liu, Haimei; Wang, Yonggang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), as one of the potential candidates for grid-scale energy storage systems, are required to tackle extreme weather conditions.  However, the all-weather SIBs with a wide operation-temp. range are rarely reported.  Herein, we propose a wide-temp. range SIB, which involves a carbon-coated Na4Fe3(PO4)2P2O7 (NFPP@C) cathode, a bismuth (Bi) anode, and a diglyme-based electrolyte.  We demonstrate that solvated Na+ can be directly stored by the Bi anode via an alloying reaction without the de-solvent process.  Furthermore, the NFPP@C cathode exhibits a high Na+ diffusion coeff. at low temp.  As a result, the Bi//NFPP@C battery exhibits perfect low-temp. behavior.  Even at -70 °C, this battery still delivers 70.19 % of the room-temp. capacity.  Furthermore, benefitting from the high b.p. of the electrolyte, this battery also works well at a high temp. of up to 100 °C.  These results are encouraging for the further exploration of wide-temp. range SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGomH1y_VNTitLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lin6Yi7tG2Cuw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XislGks7c%253D&amp;md5=ce4975a1558c0ef83e712cc28502797b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202111074"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bridging Evolution of the Solvation Sheath to Rigid-Soft Coupling and Low-Resistance Solid Electrolyte Interface for Fast-Charging and Ultrastable Bi Anode</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic bismuth has drawn attention as a promising alloying anode for advanced potassium ion batteries (PIBs).  However, serious vol. expansion/electrode pulverization and sluggish kinetics always lead to its inferior cycling and rate properties for practical applications.  Therefore, advanced Bi-based anodes via structural/compositional optimization and sur-/interface design are needed.  Herein, we develop a bottom-up avenue to fabricate nanoscale Bi encapsulated in a 3D N-doped carbon nanocages (Bi@N-CNCs) framework with a void space by using a novel Bi-based metal-org. framework as the precursor.  With elaborate regulation in annealing temps., the optimized Bi@N-CNCs electrode exhibits large reversible capacities and long-duration cyclic stability at high rates when evaluated as competitive anodes for PIBs.  Insights into the intrinsic K+-storage processes of the Bi@N-CNCs anode are put forward from comprehensive in situ characterizations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGotcuoF939HorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8agTY3JqVEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXktVOksbg%253D&amp;md5=4db97533e4d20441c8bc786855c0f8a3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1002/eem2.12130"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dang, L.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pam, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Aq. alk. battery represents a promising energy storage technol. with both high energy d. and high power d. as rechargeable batteries.  However, the low theor. capacities, kinetics and stability of anode materials have limited their developments and commercializations.  In this study, we propose a novel method to produce two-dimensional layered bismuth oxide selenium (Bi2O2Se) and reduced graphene oxide (rGO) composites via a one-step hydrothermal method.  The vol. change caused by phase change during rapid charging and discharging is significantly reduced and the capacity reaches 263.83 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1.  The Bi2O2Se/rGO electrode exhibits excellent cycling stability in which the capacity retention rate is 81.04% after 5000 cycles.  More importantly, the Bi2O2Se/rGO nanosheet composite is used as the anode electrode material with MnCo2O4.5@Ni(OH)2 as the cathode electrode material in aq. alk. battery.  When the energy d. is 76.16 W h kg-1, the power d. reaches 308.65 W kg-1.  At a power d. of 10.21 kW kg-1, the energy d. remains as high as 33.86 W h kg-1.  The results presented here may advance the understanding of the issues facing the development of aq. battery anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4opNMgMfcKLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8agTY3JqVEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhvVaisrrL&amp;md5=1347908192562026e880a0ee2b835e39</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202401833"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huo, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile galvanic replacement construction of Bi@C nanosheets array as binder-free anodes for superior sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Bi has emerged as a promising anode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs), owing to its high capacity and suitable operating potential.  However, large vol. changes during alloying/dealloying processes lead to poor cycling performance.  Here, Bi nanoparticle@C (Bi@C) composite is prepd. via a facile annealing method using a com. coordination compd. precursor of Bi citrate.  The composite has a uniform structure with Bi nanoparticles embedded within a C framework.  The nanosized structure ensures a fast kinetics and efficient alleviation of stress/strain caused by the vol. change, and the resilient and conductive C matrix provides an interconnected electron transportation pathway.  The Bi@C composite delivers outstanding Na-storage performance with an ultralong cycle life of 30,000 cycles at a high c.d. of 8 A/g and an excellent rate capability of 71% capacity retention at an ultrahigh current rate of 60 A/g.  Even at a high mass loading of 11.5 mg/cm2, a stable reversible capacity of 280 mAh/g can be obtained after 200 cycles.  Full SIBs by pairing with a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode demonstrates superior performance.  Combining the facile synthesis and the com. precursor, the exceptional performance makes the Bi@C composite very promising for practical large-scale applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGphFbJVR5Fy-rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8agTY3JqVEA"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Multi-heteroatoms co-doped carbon coating can significantly enhance the electronic cond. and mass transfer rate of the electrode materials due to the synergistic effect.  In this study N, S co-doped carbon coating is introduced on the surface of niobium oxides (GNO@NSC) by using a convenient thiourea evapn. method.  Theory calcns. and exptl. results confirm the synergistic effect of N, S co-doping in GNO@NSC composite.  N, S co-doping not only enlarges the layer distance of the carbon materials but also leads to more activation sites for lithium storage; meanwhile, the introduction of the co-doping carbon layer on GNO significantly enhances the bonding interaction with GNO, leading to excellent structural stability and cond. of the composite.  As a result, the GNO@NSC composite possesses excellent structural reversibility, a large specific capacity, and high-rate performance.  GNO@NSC nanowires deliver a highly reversible capacity of 288 mAh g-1 and display excellent cycling stability, and its capacity retention is 78.9% after 6000 cycles at a high c.d. of 1 A g-1.  This study reveals the functional mechanism of N, S co-doped carbon coating and the origin of performance improvement of niobium oxides, which can be used for ref. to design and develop relevant materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5epi5um-ry7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8agTY3JqVEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXls1WjtrY%253D&amp;md5=8ec0794df426ff7add2a001804f25a59</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1002/advs.202200247"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zuo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-Sacrifice template construction of uniform yolk-shell ZnS@C for superior alkali-ion storage</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Secondary batteries have been widespread in the daily life causing an ever-growing demand for long-cycle lifespan and high-energy alkali-ion batteries.  As an essential constituent part, electrode materials with superior electrochem. properties play a vital role in the battery systems.  Here, an outstanding electrode of yolk-shell ZnS@C nanorods is developed, introducing considerable void space via a self-sacrificial template method.  Such carbon encapsulated nanorods moderate integral electronic cond., thus ensuring rapid alkali-ions/electrons transporting.  Furthermore, the porous structure of these nanorods endows enough void space to mitigate vol. stress caused by the insertion/extn. of alkali-ions.  Due to the unique structure, these yolk-shell ZnS@C nanorods achieve superior rate performance and cycling performance (740 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 after 540 cycles) for lithium-ion batteries.  As a potassium-ion batteries anode, they achieve an ultra-long lifespan delivering 211.1 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 after 5700 cycles.  The kinetic anal. reveals that these ZnS@C nanorods with considerable pseudocapacitive contribution benefit the fast lithiation/delithiation.  Detailed transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and X-ray diffraction (XRD) analyses indicate that such yolk-shell ZnS@C anode is a typical reversible conversion reaction mechanism accomplished by alloying processes.  This rational design strategy opens a window for the development of superior energy storage materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsbXOwk52PPLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8agTY3JqVEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhtVGksrjN&amp;md5=c6c7668dabe1877f8665019326292469</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1007/s40820-022-00893-7"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Molybdenum oxynitride atomic nanoclusters bonded in nanosheets of N-doped carbon hierarchical microspheres for efficient sodium storage</span>. <i>Nano-Micro Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">163</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
